Action: free_search(query="2025 macroeconomic outlook for US consumer staples and retail sector")

Observation: The **2025 macroeconomic outlook for the US consumer staples and retail sector** is broadly stable, with several key themes shaping the environment:

**Macroeconomic Backdrop and Consumer Health**
- **Economic Growth:** US real GDP is forecast to grow by 2.4% in 2025, supporting stable consumer demand.
- **Consumer Fundamentals:** Consumer balance sheets remain strong, employment rates are healthy, and real wage growth is steady, all of which underpin robust demand for consumer staples and support retail spending.
- **Fed Policy:** The Federal Reserve has begun to cut rates, which is creating a supportive backdrop for both sectors.

**Consumer Staples Sector**
- **Return to Normal:** The consumer staples sector is expected to see a "return to normal," benefiting from the stable macroeconomic environment and resilient consumer demand.
- **Defensive Characteristics:** As a defensive sector, consumer staples have historically performed well during periods of economic uncertainty or slower growth. If broader economic growth falls short of optimistic expectations, staples may outperform.
- **Risks:** Potential changes in trade policy following the presidential election could impact input costs. While most staples are produced domestically, products with international components (e.g., packaging, some appliances) could see price increases if tariffs rise. A stronger US dollar could also pressure companies with significant international exposure.

**Retail Sector**
- **Sales Outlook:** The National Retail Federation (NRF) forecasts US retail sales growth of **2.7% to 3.7%** in 2025, reaching between **$5.42 trillion and $5.48 trillion**. This is in line with long-term pre-pandemic averages and follows 3.6% growth in 2024.
- **Consumer Spending:** Deloitte projects consumer spending will grow by 3.1% in 2025, with durable goods spending particularly strong at 4.7%.
- **E-commerce:** Online and non-store sales are projected to grow between 7% and 9% year-over-year, reflecting ongoing digital adoption and omnichannel strategies.
- **Real Estate Dynamics:** Despite thousands of store closures in 2024, retail space remains tight (4–5% vacancy) and rents are at record highs. Investment activity has stabilized, with cap rates in the 6–7% range.
- **Innovation and Omnichannel:** Retailers are investing in AI-driven inventory management, personalization, and seamless digital/physical integration to cater to evolving consumer preferences, especially among Gen Z and millennials.

**Risks and Uncertainties**
- **Policy and Trade:** Policy uncertainty, particularly around tariffs and trade, is a key risk. Significant tariff increases could slow growth and impact input costs, especially for imported goods and goods with international supply chains.
- **Consumer Confidence:** While fundamentals are strong, policy uncertainty is weighing on consumer and business confidence, which could moderate spending if conditions deteriorate.

**Summary Table: 2025 US Consumer Staples and Retail Sector Outlook**

| Indicator                      | Consumer Staples         | Retail Sector                     |
|-------------------------------|-------------------------|-----------------------------------|
| Sector Growth                  | Stable, return to normal| 2.7%–3.7% sales growth forecasted |
| Consumer Health                | Strong, steady demand   | Strong, wage gains, low unemployment |
| Policy Risk                    | Trade/tariff uncertainty| Trade/tariff uncertainty          |
| E-commerce/Omnichannel         | Moderate adoption       | 7%–9% online sales growth         |
| Real Estate                    | Not a primary driver    | Tight vacancy, high rents         |
| Defensive/Pro-cyclical         | Defensive characteristics| Pro-cyclical but resilient        |

**Key Takeaways**
- **Both sectors are underpinned by a healthy consumer and a stable economic environment.**
- **Consumer staples may outperform if macro conditions weaken, while retail is expected to see moderate growth in line with historical averages.**
- **The main uncertainties lie in trade policy, the dollar, and potential shifts post-election.**
- **Ongoing digital transformation and investment in omnichannel capabilities remain central to retail sector growth.**

This outlook suggests a cautiously optimistic scenario, with stable growth but heightened attention to external risks and continued adaptation to changing consumer behaviors.

Observation: In 2025, several key areas have generated **negative news and significant public concern** in the United States, primarily centered on **immigration policy, federal governance proposals, and civil liberties**.

**1. Immigration Policy and Administration Actions**
- **Deportations and Asylum:** The Trump administration's immigration actions have received **mixed to negative public views**. Majorities across political lines perceive an increase in deportations and a decrease in asylum-seekers compared to the previous year. Notably, 48% of Americans now believe Trump's actions as president are worse than expected, up from 35% earlier in the year.
- **Border Policy:** While support for expanding the U.S.-Mexico border wall has grown (56% overall, with rising Democratic support), there remains widespread disapproval of policies such as suspending asylum applications and local law enforcement aiding deportations.
- **Project 2025 Proposals:** The policy blueprint known as Project 2025 includes plans for **mass deportations, ending birthright citizenship, family separations, and dismantling the asylum system**. These proposals have been heavily criticized by civil rights organizations for their potential to harm immigrant communities and undermine due process protections.

**2. Radical Federal Policy Proposals (Project 2025)**
- **Education Overhaul:** Project 2025 recommends **dismantling the U.S. Department of Education**, eliminating key federal programs for low-income and disabled students, and rescinding civil rights protections for LGBTQ+ students. These ideas have been described by analysts as "outrageous" and likely to inflict harm on students and public education nationwide.
- **Civil Rights and Government Oversight:** The agenda includes plans to **reduce federal enforcement of civil rights laws** and to privatize the federal student loan portfolio, which would shift more responsibility onto states and private entities, potentially increasing inequality.
- **Executive Power Expansion:** Project 2025 outlines a dramatic expansion of executive power, including the **abuse of warrantless surveillance** and the removal of guardrails that limit presidential authority. This has raised alarms among privacy and civil liberties advocates.

**3. Public Trust and Media Disinformation**
- The Department of Homeland Security has reported a **significant increase in assaults on ICE officers** (up 300%) and has actively combated disinformation in the media, highlighting the contentious and polarized environment around enforcement operations and public debate.

**Summary Table: Main Areas of Negative News (2025)**

| Issue Area             | Key Concerns Raised                                            | Public/Expert Sentiment          |
|------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------|
| Immigration Policy     | Increased deportations, reduced asylum, mass deportation plans| Mixed to negative          |

Observation: Several recent warnings and cautious outlooks regarding **2025 financial performance** have emerged, reflecting both macroeconomic and company-specific concerns.

**Macroeconomic and Systemic Warnings**

- The **Bank of Canada’s 2025 Financial Stability Report** highlights significant systemic risks stemming from ongoing global trade tensions. Since the change in the US administration in early 2025, trade policy volatility and the risk of a prolonged trade war have increased. In their downside scenario (not a forecast, but an illustrative risk case), a persistent trade war could trigger a year-long recession in Canada, with elevated unemployment and temporary inflation above 3%. The report identifies two main risk channels:
  - **Debt-serviceability risk:** Increased credit defaults among borrowers.
  - **Liquidity risk:** Potential for substantial liquidity draws from asset managers during market stress.
  These factors could amplify any downturn and test overall financial stability.

- Commentary from financial analysts and market observers has also cautioned about **recession risks in 2025**. One widely-shared message is the importance of personal and corporate financial discipline, particularly emphasizing increased savings and conservative balance sheet management in anticipation of heightened volatility or potential economic contraction.

**Company-Level Signals and Guidance**

- **Tractor Supply Company** has adjusted its fiscal year 2025 outlook, widening its sales forecast range and providing more conservative guidance. While net sales are still expected to grow (+4% to +8%), the company has moderated its comparable store sales growth outlook (+0% to +4%), reflecting uncertainty in consumer demand and macro conditions.

- **Medtronic** continues to forecast full-year 2025 EPS in the $5.44 to $5.50 range, but notes a significant negative impact from foreign exchange (-5%) and acknowledges unfavorable revenue adjustments due to regulatory, currency, and market challenges.

- **VERB Technology** delivered strong Q1 2025 results, beating analyst estimates and posting 80% quarter-over-quarter revenue growth. However, the company’s management also emphasized the use of Modified EBITDA as a key performance metric, highlighting the need to exclude one-time items and non-core factors to better understand underlying business performance. This signals a heightened focus on operational discipline as the economic environment becomes more challenging.

**Key Takeaways for 2025 Financial Performance:**

- **Trade policy uncertainty** and the potential for a prolonged trade war are material risks for global and national economies, with possible recessionary implications.
- **Companies are expressing caution** in their guidance, adjusting forecasts, and emphasizing operational efficiency and risk management.
- **Financial analysts and central banks** urge increased vigilance, readiness for potential credit and liquidity shocks, and prudent financial planning at all levels.

Given these signals, investors and corporate decision-makers should closely monitor evolving macroeconomic indicators, company guidance updates, and policy developments throughout 2025.
